Allah's Existence
beginner
6 min
Classification of Existents: Necessary and Possible
The author classifies existents into necessary and possible, then subdivides possible beings into four categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how all existents are divided into the necessary-by-itself (God) and the possible-by-itself (everything else), and how possible beings are further categorized into four divisions based on their mode of subsistence and spatiality.

Core Idea
All existence is either necessary by itself (God) or possible by itself (creation), and the possible is divided into four kinds.

This passage establishes the foundational classification of all reality into two fundamental categories: the Necessary Being, who is God, and every other existent, which is possible in itself. From there, the author subdivides the possible into four distinct types based on whether they are self-subsistent or subsist through another, and whether they occupy space or not. This taxonomy is essential for understanding the nature of created beings, from physical bodies to spiritual substances.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the author's classification. Notice the compact style and the logical flow from broadest category to specific examples.
2
Identify the primary division
Note the initial split into wājib bi-dhātihi (necessary by itself) and mumkin bi-dhātihi (possible by itself). Understand that the necessary is God, who must be non-spatial and not inhering in anything spatial.
The condition for God is given after the primary division.
3
Trace the subdivisions of the possible
Follow the branching of possible into self-subsistent vs. subsistent through another, then each into spatial and non-spatial. Count the four resulting categories.
The author explicitly says 'these are four divisions' (فهذه أقسام أربعة).
4
Understand the application
See how these categories correspond to actual entities: spatial essences and attributes are known to be real; non-spatial essences are called separated entities (mufāriqāt) or spirits (arwāh), and are further divided into detached intellects and attached spirits.
This connects the abstract classification to concrete realities.
5
Reflect on the purpose
Recognize that this classification is the basis for discussing the existence and attributes of God and the nature of spiritual beings. It sets the stage for the rest of the book.
The author's aim is to detail the doctrines of people regarding these existents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول
في
تفصيل مذاهب الناس فيهـ
اعلم : أن الموجود . إما أن يكون واجباً لذاته ، وإما أن يكون ممكناً لذاته . أما الواجب لذاته فهو الله جل جلاله . وأطبق المحققون على أنه يجب أن يكون ، لا متحيزاً ، ولا حالا في المتحيز . وأما الممكن لذاته . فإما أن يكون قائماً بالنفس ، وإما أن يكون قائماً بالغير، والقائم بالنفس . إما أن يكون متحيزاً ، وإما أن لا يكون متحيزاً . والقائم بالغير . إما أن يكون قائماً بالمتحيز ، وإما أن يكون قائماً بغير المتحيز . فهذه أقسام أربعة
·
فأما الذوات المتحيزة والصفات القائمة ، فهي معلومة الثبوت . وأما الذوات التي لا تكون متحيزة فهي المسماة في اصطلاح الفلاسفة بالمفارقات .. وفي اصطلاح قوم آخرين بالأرواح. وهي على قسمين . لأن هذه الذوات . إما أن يقال : كما أنها ليست أجساماً ، ولا حالة في الأجسام ، فكذلك ليست متعلقة بالأجسام على سبيل التصرف والتدبير [ وإما أن يقال : إنها متعلقة بالأجسام على سبيل التصرف والتدبير ] والأول تسميها الفلاسفة بالعقول المجردة .
Chapter One: Detailing the doctrines of people concerning them. Know that the existent is either necessary by itself or possible by itself. As for the necessary by itself, it is God, exalted be His majesty. And the investigators have agreed that He must be neither occupying space nor inhering in what occupies space. As for the possible by itself, it is either self-subsistent or subsistent through another. The self-subsistent is either occupying space or not occupying space. The subsistent through another is either subsisting in what occupies space or subsisting in what does not occupy space. These are four divisions. As for the occupying-space essences and the subsisting attributes, they are known to be established. As for the essences that are not occupying space, they are called in the terminology of the philosophers 'separated entities' (al-mufāriqāt) and in the terminology of others 'spirits' (al-arwāḥ). They are of two types: these essences are either said, just as they are not bodies nor states in bodies, so also they are not attached to bodies by way of disposal and management; or they are said to be attached to bodies by way of disposal and management. The first the philosophers call 'disembodied intellects' (al-ʿuqūl al-mujarrada).
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is a fundamental classification of all existents (al-mawjūd). The author begins by dividing existents into two primary categories: the necessary by itself (wājib bi-dhātihi) and the possible by itself (mumkin bi-dhātihi). The necessary by itself is God, and the author notes the consensus of investigators (muḥaqqiqūn) that God must be neither spatial (mutaḥayyiz) nor inhering in a spatial entity (ḥāll fī al-mutaḥayyiz). This establishes God's transcendence above physicality.

The second category, the possible by itself, is further subdivided. First, it is divided into that which is self-subsistent (qāʾim bi-nafs) and that which subsists through another (qāʾim bi-al-ghayr). The self-subsistent can either occupy space (mutaḥayyiz) or not occupy space. The subsistent through another can either subsist in a spatial entity (qāʾim bi-al-mutaḥayyiz) or subsist in a non-spatial entity (qāʾim bi-ghayr al-mutaḥayyiz). The author states that these are four divisions, which are the four categories of possible beings.

Then the author applies these divisions to actual entities. The essences that occupy space (al-dhawāt al-mutaḥayyiza) and the attributes that subsist (al-ṣifāt al-qāʾima) are known to be real. The essences that do not occupy space are called 'separated entities' (al-mufāriqāt) by philosophers and 'spirits' (al-arwāḥ) by others. These non-spatial essences are of two types: those that are not attached to bodies at all for disposal and management, and those that are attached to bodies for disposal and management. The first type—those detached from bodies—are called by the philosophers 'disembodied intellects' (al-ʿuqūl al-mujarrada). This sets the stage for the discussion of higher and lower spirits, which is the subject of the book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that 'possible by itself' implies something that can come into existence or perish, but here it includes all created beings, both material and spiritual, that are not necessary in themselves.
Correction: In this classification, 'possible by itself' (mumkin bi-dhātihi) means any being that is not necessary in its own essence, i.e., all of creation. It includes both contingent and eternal created things (like spirits). The term does not imply temporal origination, but rather ontological dependence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, into how many divisions does the possible by itself (الممكن لذاته) fall?
A) Two divisions
B) Three divisions
C) Four divisions
D) Five divisions

Key Takeaway
All of creation can be classified into four categories based on whether it is self-subsistent or dependent, and whether it is material or non-material.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are a possible being, not necessary. Your existence depends entirely on God's will at every moment. How does this truth affect your attitude toward your own achievements and failures today? Will you consciously acknowledge your contingency in your next action?
?
If God alone is necessary, then everything else—your health, wealth, relationships—could vanish in an instant. Are you clinging to any of these as if they were necessary? What is one attachment you can loosen today in recognition of God's sole necessity?
?
The lesson describes spirits that are attached to bodies (like your soul) and those that are detached (disembodied intellects). Which category describes you now? How does your current attachment to your body affect your awareness of your ultimate dependence on God? What one step can you take today to prioritize your spiritual reality over bodily desires?

Proof that Allah Affects and Is Not Affected
Proves that Allah belongs to the second division (affects and is not affected) using necessary existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that Allah, as the Necessary Being, cannot be affected by anything external, based on the necessity of His essence and attributes.

Core Idea
Allah's necessary existence makes His attributes immutable and impervious to external influence.

This passage from al-Matālib al-Āliyya presents a logical proof that Allah alone is the one who affects and is never affected. The argument hinges on the concept of necessary existence (wujūb al-wujūd) and the necessity of all divine attributes. By examining the sufficiency of Allah's essence for His attributes, the author demonstrates that change or dependence on another is impossible for the Divine. As you read, follow the two-step reasoning: first establishing Allah's necessary existence, then proving that this necessitates immutability in all attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully along with the translation. Notice the structure: a claim followed by a proof.
The text is truncated, but the main argument is clear.
2
Identify the key premise
The author states: 'Everything necessary in essence is necessary in all its attributes.' Understand what this means for Allah's attributes.
3
Examine the sufficiency argument
The author uses a conditional: if the essence is sufficient for an attribute, then the attribute is perpetual; if not, it depends on another, which is impossible. Trace the logic and see why this proves that Allah cannot be affected.
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القسم الثاني : وهو الذي يؤثر ولا يتأثر البتة ، فهو الله سبحانه وتعالى . والدليل عليه : أنه واجب الوجود لذاته ، وكل ما كان واجباً لذاته كان واجب الوجود في جميع صفاته السلبية والثبوتية . والدليل عليه : أن ذاته المخصوصة ، إن كانت كافية في حصول ذلك الايجاب ، أو ذلك السلب ، يلزم يدوم ذلك الإيجاب . وذلك السلب بدوام ذاته . فحينئذ يمتنع وقوع التغير في شيء من صفاته ، وإن لم تكن ذاته كافية في حصول ذلك الإيجاب وذلك السلب ، فحينئذ يتوقف حصول ذلك الإيجاب ، وذلك السلب [ على اعتبار حال الغير، ولا شك أن هويته موقوفة على حصول ذلك الإيجاب أو ذلك السلب ] والموقوف على الموقوف على الغير. موقوف على الغير . والموقوف
As for the second division: that which affects and is not affected at all, it is Allah, exalted be He. The proof for that: He is necessary of existence in His essence, and everything that is necessary in its essence is necessary of existence in all its negative and positive attributes. The proof for that: that His specific essence, if it is sufficient for the occurrence of that affirmation or that negation, then that affirmation and that negation must perpetually continue with the perpetuity of His essence. Then it is impossible for change to occur in any of His attributes. And if His essence is not sufficient for the occurrence of that affirmation and that negation, then the occurrence of that affirmation and that negation depends on considering the state of another, and there is no doubt that His identity depends on the occurrence of that affirmation or that negation, and that which depends on that which depends on another depends on another. And that which depends...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a proof that Allah alone belongs to the second division: the one who affects and is never affected. The author provides a two-step argument. First, Allah is necessary of existence in His essence (wājib al-wujūd li-dhātihī). Second, anything necessary in essence is also necessary in all its attributes—both negative (salbīyya) and positive (thubūtiyya). The author then proves this by examining whether His essence is sufficient for the occurrence of any attribute. If it is sufficient, then the attribute must be perpetual and unchanging. If it is not sufficient, then the attribute would depend on something external, making the essence dependent on that attribute, which would ultimately make Allah dependent on another—impossible for the Necessary Being. Thus, Allah's attributes are immutable, and He cannot be subject to change or influence from outside, so He cannot be affected. The text cuts off before completing the second conditional, probably concluding that dependence on another is impossible.

صفات سلبية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'affecting without being affected' implies God is impassive in a way that denies His knowledge of creation.
Correction: The argument here is about ontological independence, not relational knowledge. Allah's knowledge of creation does not imply He is affected by it.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason given that Allah cannot be affected?
A) He is omnipotent
B) He is necessary of existence and His attributes are necessary and immutable
C) He is merciful
D) He is the creator

Key Takeaway
Allah, as the Necessary Being, possesses all attributes necessarily and immutably, which is why He cannot be affected by anything external.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah’s attributes are necessary and unchanging, what does that mean for the times you have doubted His mercy or justice because of your circumstances? How does the immutability of His attributes challenge your tendency to judge Him based on your changing emotions?
?
You often rely on external validation or outcomes to feel secure. But this lesson says Allah depends on nothing. Are you truly relying on Him as the Self-Sufficient, or are you expecting Him to act like a needy being? What would change in your daily trust if you internalised that He cannot be affected by your situation?
?
The proof shows that if Allah’s essence were not sufficient for His attributes, He would depend on others. But do you live as if you believe He is self-sufficient? When you sin, do you act as though you can diminish His glory? Reflect on the weight of 'He is not affected' and how it should shift your awe of Him.

Allah's Existence
intermediate
8 min
God: The Unaffected Agent Who Affects All Creation
Al-Razi proves that God alone is the active cause who is not subject to any external influence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's proof that God alone is the necessary existent who cannot be affected by anything and who actively causes all other things to exist.

Core Idea
God's necessary existence makes Him immune to change and the source of all else.

In this passage from his philosophical theology, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi establishes a crucial distinction: God is the being who affects without being affected. Building on the concept of necessary existence (wajib al-wujud), al-Razi argues that God's essence is such that all His attributes are necessary and unchanging. At the same time, everything other than God is contingent and depends on Him for its existence. This lesson unpacks that proof and its implications for understanding God as al-Qayyum, the Self-Subsisting.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with its key terms
Read the Arabic text and translation, noting the key terms like wajib al-wujud, mumkin al-wujud, and the categories of attributes (salbiyya and thubutiyya).
The passage uses a formal argument structure.
2
Follow the proof that God is not affected
Al-Razi first argues that God's necessity entails that all His attributes are necessary, making change impossible. Work through the conditional reasoning step by step.
3
See how God affects everything else
The second part shows that all contingent things need a cause, and that cause is God. This establishes God as the active agent over all.
The conclusion identifies God with al-Qayyum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القسم الثاني : وهو الذي يؤثر ولا يتأثر البتة ، فهو الله سبحانه وتعالى . والدليل عليه : أنه واجب الوجود لذاته ، وكل ما كان واجباً لذاته كان واجب الوجود في جميع صفاته السلبية والثبوتية . والدليل عليه : أن ذاته المخصوصة ، إن كانت كافية في حصول ذلك الايجاب ، أو ذلك السلب ، يلزم يدوم ذلك الإيجاب . وذلك السلب بدوام ذاته . فحينئذ يمتنع وقوع التغير في شيء من صفاته ، وإن لم تكن ذاته كافية في حصول ذلك الايجاب وذلك السلب ، فحينئذ يتوقف حصول ذلك الايجاب ، وذلك السلب [ على اعتبار حال الغير، ولا شك أن هويته موقوفة على حصول ذلك الايجاب أو ذلك السلب ] والموقوف على الموقوف على الغير. موقوف على الغير . والموقوف على الغير ] : ممكن لذاته [ فواجب الوجود لذاته ، ممكن الوجود لذاته ] هذا خلف . فثبت : أن الحق سبحانه وتعالى ؛ واجب الوجود لذاته ، وواجب الوجود في كل صفاته الإيجابية والسلبية ] وكل ما كان كذلك، فهو لا يقبل الأثر من الغير البتة . وأما بيان أنه مؤثر في غيره ، فهو أنه ثبت : أن كل ما عدا الموجود الواحد الواجب ، فإنه ممكن لذاته، وكل ممكن لذاته، فإنه لا يوجد إلا بإيجاد الواجب لذاته. إما بواسطة أو بغير واسطة . فثبت : أن الحق سبحانه وتعالى : مؤثر في كل ما سواه ، وأنه لا يقبل الأثر البتة عن شيء مما سواه . فهو من حيث أنه مستقل في وجوده ، وفي جميع صفاته الثبوتية والسلبية . قائم بنفسه ومن حيث إن كل ما سواه [ قائم به ] فإنه يوجد بإيجاده . وإن ما يتقوم بتقويمه ، فهو مقوم بغيره . والكامل في كونه قائماً بذاته ، مقوماً لغيره : هو الله القيوم . فواجب الوجود : هو القيوم الحق . فلهذا السر قال في الكتاب الأنمي : ( الله لا إله إلا هو ، الحي القيوم )
As for the second division: that which affects and is not affected at all, it is Allah—glorified and exalted is He. The proof for it: that He is necessary of existence by His essence, and everything that is necessary by its essence is necessary of existence in all its negative and positive attributes. The proof for that: that His specific essence, if it is sufficient for the occurrence of that affirmation or that negation, then that affirmation and that negation must persist with the persistence of the essence. Then change in any of His attributes is impossible. But if His essence is not sufficient for the occurrence of that affirmation and that negation, then the occurrence of that affirmation and that negation depends on consideration of the state of another, and undoubtedly His identity depends on the occurrence of that affirmation or that negation. That which depends on what depends on another depends on another. And what depends on another is possible by its essence. So [if] necessary of existence by essence were possible of existence by essence, this is a contradiction. So it is established that the Truth—glorified and exalted is He—is necessary of existence by His essence, and necessary of existence in all His positive and negative attributes. And everything that is like that does not accept influence from another at all. As for the explanation that He affects others, it is that it is established that everything other than the one necessary existent is possible by its essence, and every possible by its essence does not exist except by the bringing into existence of the necessary by His essence, either through an intermediary or without an intermediary. So it is established that the Truth—glorified and exalted is He—affects everything other than Him, and that He does not accept influence at all from anything other than Him. So He, in terms of being independent in His existence and in all His positive and negative attributes, is self-subsisting; and in terms that everything other than Him subsists by Him, it exists by His bringing into existence. And what is constituted by His constituting is constituted by another. And the perfect in being self-subsisting and constituting others is Allah, the Self-Subsisting (al-Qayyum). So the necessary of existence is the True Self-Subsisting. For this secret He said in the Book al-Anmi: 'Allah—there is no god but He, the Living, the Self-Subsisting.'
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation of the first category from the previous classification: God is the one who affects without being affected. The author provides two arguments: first, to show He is not affected; second, to show He affects others. For the first: God is necessary of existence (wajib al-wujud) by His essence. Necessity implies that all His attributes—both negative (salbiyya) and positive (thubutiyya)—are likewise necessary. The proof proceeds by considering whether His essence suffices for those attributes or not. If it does, the attributes are permanent and unchangeable. If not, then the attributes depend on something else, making His identity dependent, which contradicts necessary existence. Thus, He cannot receive influence. For the second: All else is possible (mumkin), needing a cause; that cause is God. Hence He affects all else. The passage concludes by identifying God with al-Qayyum, the Self-Subsisting upon Whom all depend, and cites the Ayat al-Kursi.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
ممكن الوجود
صفات سلبية
صفات ثبوتية
قيوم
ذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's being unaffected means He is passive or remote from creation.
Correction: The passage shows that God's being unaffected is due to His necessary existence, but He actively affects all creation as the sole agent.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, why can God not be affected by anything?
A) Because He is too powerful to be affected
B) Because His essence is necessary and all His attributes are necessary, making change impossible
C) Because He has no attributes that could be affected
D) Because He is a spirit

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi proves that God alone is the necessary existent who, because of His necessity, cannot be affected and is the cause of all contingent existence, which is the meaning of al-Qayyum.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God is truly unaffected by your actions, do you still pray as if you can change His mind, or do you surrender to His eternal decree? Where do you see your lack of trust in His perfect plan?
?
You confess that everything depends on God, yet where in your life do you cling to a false sense of control—your career, relationships, or health? Will you consciously attribute one decision today entirely to His causation?
?
Al-Razi proves that God alone is the active cause. In what area of your life have you been acting as if you are self-sufficient? What would change if you truly lived knowing you are completely dependent on al-Qayyum?

Allah's Existence
intermediate
6 min
God as Necessary Existent and the Source of All
Al-Razi proves God's necessity and causal role via reductio and dependency argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi argues that God is both necessary in Himself and the sole source of existence for everything else, while remaining completely unaffected.

Core Idea
God is the only one who is self-necessitating, and all else depends entirely on Him.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi builds a crisp philosophical proof that God is the Necessary Existent, drawing a sharp contrast between His self-sufficiency and the dependence of everything else. He uses a reductio argument to show that to be both necessary and possible is contradictory, then demonstrates that God alone is both self-subsistent and the cause of all other beings. As you read the text, notice how the concepts of necessity and possibility are used to establish God's uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without pausing to analyze. Then read the translation to get the full argument flow. Notice that the passage moves from a logical contradiction to two positive conclusions.
The style is dense but logical. Pay attention to the phrase 'هذا خلف' — that's the key to the reductio.
2
Identify the first conclusion
The passage first establishes that God is Wajib al-Wujud (Necessary Existent) in Himself and in all attributes. Ask: why does necessity exclude the possibility of being affected?
The text says 'فهو لا يقبل الأثر من الغير البتة' — He does not accept effect at all.
3
Follow the second proof
The second part shows that everything else is possible and thus needs a cause, which is God. Notice that He can cause directly or indirectly, yet remains untouched.
The phrase 'إما بواسطة أو بغير واسطة' shows the causal chain ultimately ends at God.
4
Connect to the name al-Qayyum
The passage concludes by linking these attributes to the divine name al-Qayyum, 'the Self-Subsisting by Whom all subsist'. See how the Quranic verse reinforces the argument.
The verse 'Allah, there is no god but He, the Living, the Self-Sustaining' is cited as a revealed confirmation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على الغير : ممكن لذاته فواجب الوجود لذاته، ممكن الوجود لذاته هذا خلف. فثبت: أن الحق سبحانه وتعالى واجب الوجود لذاته، وواجب الوجود في كل صفاته الإيجابية والسلبية. وكل ما كان كذلك، فهو لا يقبل الأثر من الغير البتة. وأما بيان أنه مؤثر في غيره، فهو أنه ثبت: أن كل ما عدا الموجود الواحد الواجب، فإنه ممكن لذاته، وكل ممكن لذاته، فإنه لا يوجد إلا بإيجاد الواجب لذاته. إما بواسطة أو بغير واسطة. فثبت: أن الحق سبحانه وتعالى مؤثر في كل ما سواه، وأنه لا يقبل الأثر البتة عن شيء مما سواه. فهو من حيث أنه مستقل في وجوده، وفي جميع صفاته الثبوتية والسلبية. قائم بنفسه ومن حيث إن كل ما سواه قائم به فإنه يوجد بإيجاده. وإن ما يتقوم بتقويمه، فهو مقوم بغيره. والكامل في كونه قائماً بذاته، مقوماً لغيره: هو الله القيوم. فواجب الوجود: هو القيوم الحق. فلهذا السر قال في الكتاب الأنمي: (الله لا إله إلا هو، الحي القيوم)
on the other: possible in itself, so the Necessary of Existence in itself, the possible of existence in itself – this is a contradiction. So it is established that the Truth, glorified and exalted, is Necessary of Existence in Himself, and Necessary of Existence in all His positive and negative attributes. And everything that is such, He does not accept effect from another at all. As for the explanation that He is effective in others, it is that it is established: that everything other than the one Necessary Existent is possible in itself, and every possible in itself does not exist except by the bringing into existence of the Necessary in Himself. Either through an intermediary or without an intermediary. So it is established that the Truth, glorified and exalted, is effective in everything other than Him, and that He does not accept effect at all from anything other than Him. So He, in that He is independent in His existence and in all His positive and negative attributes, is self-subsistent, and in that everything other than Him is subsistent by Him, it exists by His bringing into existence. And that which is constituted by His constitution, He is the Constitutor of others. And the perfect in being self-subsistent and constituting others is Allah, al-Qayyum. So the Necessary of Existence is al-Qayyum, the Truth. For this secret He said in the book al-anami: 'Allah – there is no deity except Him, the Ever-Living, the Self-Sustaining.'
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is a proof that God is the Necessary Existent and that He alone is truly effective while being unaffected. It begins with a reductio ad absurdum: if something were both necessary and possible in itself, it would be contradictory. Thus, God is established as Wajib al-Wujud (Necessary Existent) in Himself and in all His attributes. Since necessity excludes passivity, He cannot receive effect from any other. The proof then shows that everything else is possible (mumkin li-dhatihi) and therefore requires an efficient cause. That cause is God, who brings them into existence either directly or indirectly. Consequently, God is mu'aththir (effective) in all that is other than Him. The passage then describes God as independent (qaim bi nafsihi) and as the one through whom all else subsists (qaim bihi). The perfect example of this is Allah, described as al-Qayyum, and the Quranic verse (2:255) is cited to reinforce this attribute.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
ممكن لذاته
مؤثر
قائم بنفسه
القيوم
قائم به

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that God needs creation to act or that He can be affected by His creatures.
Correction: This passage proves that because God is necessary in Himself and in all attributes, He cannot receive any effect from another. Moreover, He is the sole source of existence for all others, so they depend on Him, not vice versa.

Checkpoint
Why can the Necessary Existent not be affected by anything else according to this passage?
A) Because He is eternal and unchanging.
B) Because He is Necessary in Himself and in all His attributes, so He cannot receive effect.
C) Because He is all-powerful and chooses not to be affected.
D) Because He is the creator of all things.

Key Takeaway
God is the only necessary being, unaffected by anything, and the cause of all existence, perfectly described by the name al-Qayyum.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi proves that God is absolutely independent and unaffected by anything. In your life, where do you act as if you are self-sufficient, seeking approval or fearing others' opinions more than God's? Identify one such area and commit today to consciously rely on God alone.
?
You are a possible being, and every moment you exist only because God brings you into existence. Do you truly live with this awareness, or do you take your existence for granted? What specific action can you take today to acknowledge your constant dependence on al-Qayyum?
?
If God is the only true cause and you are merely an instrument, what does that mean for your sense of control and worry? How would your anxiety change if you deeply believed that nothing happens except by His causation? Write down one worry you can release to God today.

The Threefold Classification of Existents
The author classifies existents into three categories and states the nobility of existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how existence is ranked by nobility based on causality, and the three categories of existents: the effectual unaffected, the affected non-effectual, and the both effectual and affected.

Core Idea
Existence is noble, and its nobility is measured by causal power.

This passage introduces a fundamental classification of all existents into three kinds based on whether they effect (cause) or are affected. The author begins by asserting that existence itself is nobler than non-existence, then ranks existents by their causal agency. This classification sets the stage for understanding the nature of spirits and souls in relation to God and matter.

Guided Path
1
Read and translate the passage
Read the Arabic passage once for flow, then read the literal translation. Note the tripartite structure highlighted by 'أما' (as for).
The word 'وأخها' is unclear in the OCR; it likely means 'and its counterpart'.
2
Identify the three categories
List the three categories: 1) المؤثر الذي لا يتأثر (the effectual unaffected) – God; 2) المتأثر الذي لا يؤثر (the affected non-effectual) – matter; 3) الذي يؤثر ويتأثر معاً (that which effects and is affected together) – spirits and souls.
Notice the rank: from noblest (God) to lowest (matter), with an intermediate.
3
Reflect on the ranking principle
Understand why existence is considered noble: because the noblest existent has pure causality (unaffected), while the least is purely passive. The middle combines both.
This principle will be used later to examine the nature of spirits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا عرفت هذا، فنقول: ( من الظاهر ) أن الوجود أشرف من العدم، ولهذا السبب كان أشرف الموجودات : المؤثر الذي لا يتأثر ، وهو الله سبحانه وتعالى وأخها : المتأثر الذي لا يؤثر ، وهو الهيولى . وأما القسم الثالث من أقسام الموجودات : وهو الذي يؤثر ويتأثر معاً . فهو عالم الأرواح والنفوس
When you know this, we say: It is apparent that existence is nobler than non-existence, and for this reason the noblest of existents is the effectual which is not affected, and that is God, may He be exalted, and its counterpart [?] is the affected which does not effect, and that is matter (hayula). As for the third division of existents, which is that which effects and is affected together, it is the world of spirits and souls.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a classification of existents based on the terms 'effectual' (mu'aththir) and 'affected' (muta'aththir). The author begins by stating that existence is nobler than non-existence, a premise used to rank existents. The noblest existent is the one that influences others but is not influenced: God. The opposite is the one that is influenced but does not influence: prime matter (hayula). The intermediate category comprises beings that both influence and are influenced: spirits and souls. This tripartite division sets the stage for investigating whether spirits and souls are in fact both effectual and affected, which is taken up in the following lessons.

Key Terms

عدم
مؤثر
متأثر
هيولى
أرواح
نفوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'effecting' and 'being affected' are mutually exclusive categories, so only two types exist.
Correction: The author explicitly introduces a third category that combines both, showing that causal agency and passivity can coexist.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which existent is considered the noblest?
A) The affected non-effectual
B) The unaffected effectual
C) The both effectual and affected
D) Non-existence

Key Takeaway
Existence is ranked by causal agency: the noblest is the cause unaffected (God), then the effect non‑causing (matter), and in between are causes that are also affected (spirits and souls).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage tells you that existence is inherently noble, and nobility is measured by causal power. Do you live as a cause of good in the world, or as a mere effect—reacting to circumstances, influenced by others but rarely influencing? Which category do you truly belong to?
?
God alone is the 'effectual which is not affected'—the Causer who cannot be caused. Does your heart recognize that you are always the affected one in relation to God? When you feel self-sufficient, are you not denying this truth?
?
If you are a spirit and soul that both affects and is affected, what are you currently allowing to affect you? What influences are you passively absorbing that you should be actively shaping? The passage affirms your agency—so what will you change today?

The First Matter: Proving Spirits are Affected
Sanusi proves spirits are affected using the necessary-possible distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the necessary-possible distinction proves that spirits are affected (i.e., dependent on a cause for their existence).

Core Idea
Spirits are possible existents; every possible needs a cause.

Before investigating whether spirits can act as causes, the author first establishes that they are themselves caused. He uses a foundational argument from the nature of existence: only God is necessary, all else is possible. This lesson walks you through that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the logical flow.
Pay attention to the terms 'واجب الوجود' and 'ممكن'.
2
Identify the proof structure
The argument goes: God is one and necessary, so everything else is possible; spirits are among 'everything else', so they are possible; possible things need a cause to exist; therefore spirits are affected (caused).
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The conclusion is that spirits are 'قابلة للأثر' – receptive of effect. This means they are not self-sufficient.
This sets up the second matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب البحث ههنا عن أمرين : الأول : إثبات أنها متأثرة . والدليل عليه : أن واجب الوجود لذاته : واحد ، فيكون كل ما سواه : ممكناً لذاته. فهذه الأرواح والنفوس ممكنة لذواتها . والممكن لذاته لا يوجد إلا بمؤثر ، فثبت أن هذه الأرواح قابلة للأثر الثاني : إثبات أنها مؤثرة ، وههنا [ يحصل (4) ] البحث العظيم . فمن الثاني : من زعم : أنه لا يؤثر إلا الواحد ، الذي هو واجب الوجود لذاته . واحتج (9) عليه بوجوه :
And it is necessary to investigate here two matters: The first: proving that they are affected. The proof for it is: the Necessary of Existence in itself is one, so everything other than it is possible in itself. So these spirits and souls are possible in themselves. And the possible in itself does not exist except by an effectual cause, so it is established that these spirits are receptive of effect. The second: proving that they are effectual, and here occurs the great research. Among those who deny [this] are those who claim that none effects except the One, who is the Necessary of Existence in itself. And they adduced proofs for it, which are:
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage sets out two investigative tasks concerning spirits and souls. The first task is to prove they are affected (muta'aththira), i.e., that they receive existence from another. The proof is straightforward: only God is necessary; everything else is possible; a possible existent requires a cause to bring it into existence; therefore spirits are caused (affected). The second task is to prove they are effectual (mu'aththira), i.e., that they can themselves produce effects. This is called the 'great research' because it is contested. Some opponents claim that only the One (God) can be an effectual cause. The author then notes that these opponents have several proofs, which will be listed in subsequent lessons.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود
ممكن
متأثر
أرواح
نفوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If spirits are affected, they must be completely passive and have no causal power.
Correction: The proof only shows they are dependent for their existence, not that they cannot cause effects. The second matter addresses their effectuality.

Checkpoint
What is the proof that spirits are affected?
A) They are composed of matter and form
B) They are possible in themselves and need a cause
C) They are eternal
D) They are simple

Key Takeaway
The first matter establishes that spirits are not self-existent; they depend on an effectual cause for their existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you act as if your soul is self-sufficient, and how does this proof call you to acknowledge your utter dependence on God every moment?
?
If your spirit is completely receptive of effect from God, that means every breath and every heartbeat is a direct gift. Are you truly living in constant awareness of that dependence, or do you take it for granted?
?
This proof strips away any illusion of self-subsistence. What is one specific habit, thought, or attitude you need to change today to live as someone who knows they are always 'affected' by God?

The Second Matter: Proving Spirits are Effectual
Sanusi introduces the second matter and states the opposing claim that only God is effectual.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second investigatory matter: proving that spirits are effectual, and the opposing view that only God is the true cause.

Core Idea
The great research is whether spirits can cause effects; some deny it.

Having established that spirits are themselves caused, the author turns to the more controversial question: can spirits be causes? He calls this 'the great research' and immediately identifies an opposing view: that only the Necessary Existence can be an effectual cause. This lesson sets up the debate.

This is a strong monotheistic view.

The Second Proof for Tawheed: First Division (Non-Impossible Multiple Effects)
Razi presents the first division of the second proof for tawheed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first division of the second proof for tawheed: how the possibility of multiple effects from one cause leads to affirming worship of the known God alone.

Core Idea
If multiple effects from one cause are possible, only the known effecter is certain.

Razi presents a powerful proof for tawheed by examining whether a single cause can produce multiple effects. The proof divides into two distinct cases. This lesson explores the first case: if it is not impossible for one cause to produce many effects, what follows? Razi shows that this scenario actually reinforces the necessity of worshiping only God, the known effecter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the preliminary point about the simple and the logical division.
2
Identify the logical steps
Trace the argument: assumption, known existence of Necessary Existent, attribution of all things to Him, certainty vs doubt, practical implication.
The Quranic verse supports the conclusion.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand why reason necessitates worship of the known God alone, and how the verse reinforces this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إن عندهم البسيط لا يكون قابلاً وفاعلاً معاً . الحجة الثانية : أن نقول : إن الشيء الواحد . إما أن لا يمتنع كونه مصدراً للأثرين أو يمتنع . فإن لم يمتنع ذلك ، فنقول : لا شك أن واجب الوجود لذاته : موجود . ولا شك أنه مؤثر في وجود غيره . والتقدير في هذا القسم : أنه لا يمتنع صدور الآثار الكثيرة عن المؤثر الواحد . وإذا كان لم يمتنع إسناد جميع موجودات العالم إليه . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فإثبات المؤثر الواحد : معلوم ، وإما إثبات ما عداه : فمشكوك فيه . والتمسك بطاعة المعبود المعلوم، أولى من التمسك بطاعة المعبود المجهول . فثبت : أن العقل يقتضى التوجه إلى عبادة الله تعالى ، والإعراض عن كل ما سواه وهذا الدليل هو المذكور في الكتاب الإلهي ، حيث قال تعالى : ( ومن الله إلهاً آخر ، لا برهان له به. فإنما حسابه عند ربه ) والمعنى : أن يدع مع المعبود الأول معلوم الثبوت ، وما سواه غير معلوم. والاقتصار على المعلوم أولى من الذهاب إلى غير المعلوم وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يكون التقدير ، هو أنه يمتنع صدور الآثار الكثيرة عن المؤثر الواحد ، فنقول : فعلى هذا التقدير ، يمتنع كون الممكن لذاته ، مصدراً للأثر ، لأن للممكن لذاته ماهية ، تقتضي الإمكان فلو اقتضت تلك الماهية أثراً آخر ، لزم صدور الآثار الكثيرة عن المؤثر الواحد ، وهو محال .
Second: According to them, the simple is not receptive and active together. The second proof: We say: The single thing either is not impossible for it to be a source of two effects, or it is impossible. If that is not impossible, we say: There is no doubt that the Necessary Existent in itself exists. And there is no doubt that it effects the existence of other than itself. And the assumption in this division is that it is not impossible for many effects to issue from a single effecter. And if it is not impossible to attribute all existing things of the world to it. And on this assumption, the affirmation of a single effecter is known, but the affirmation of other than it is doubtful. And adherence to obedience of the known object of worship is more appropriate than adherence to obedience of the unknown object of worship. So it is established that reason necessitates directing oneself to worship of God Almighty and turning away from everything other than Him. And this proof is mentioned in the divine book, where He said: (And whoever invokes besides God another god for which he has no proof, then his reckoning is with his Lord). And the meaning is that one should leave the first object of worship whose existence is known, and other than it is unknown. And confining oneself to the known is more appropriate than going to the unknown. As for the second division: It is that the assumption is that it is impossible for many effects to issue from a single effecter. We say: On this assumption, it is impossible for that which is possible in itself to be a source of an effect, because that which is possible in itself has an essence that necessitates possibility. So if that essence necessitated another effect, the issuance of many effects from a single effecter would follow, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a proof (the second proof) for tawheed (the oneness of God). It begins with a preliminary point stating that, according to the opponents, a simple entity cannot be both receptive and active simultaneously. Then the proof itself proceeds by dividing the issue of a single cause producing multiple effects into two possibilities: either it is not impossible or it is impossible. In the first case, the necessary existent (wajib al-wujud) is known to exist and to be an effecter of others. Since there is no impossibility in attributing all contingent things to it, affirming this single effecter is certain, while others are doubtful. Therefore, reason dictates worship of the known God alone. This is supported by the Quranic verse (23:117) which criticizes invoking another god without proof. In the second case, if it is impossible for one cause to produce multiple effects, then even a contingent thing (mumkin) cannot produce an effect, because its essence necessitates possibility, so any effect from it would require multiple effects from one cause, which is absurd. Thus, in both divisions, only one ultimate effecter remains.

Key Terms
بسيط (simple)
قابلاً (receptive)
فاعلاً (active)
مؤثر (effecter)
أثر (effect)
واجب الوجود (necessary existent)
معبود (object of worship)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the proof only works if multiple effects are impossible, but it actually covers both possibilities and still proves monotheism.
Correction: The proof explicitly considers both scenarios and shows that even when multiple effects are not impossible, monotheism is still demanded by reason.

Checkpoint
According to the first division of the proof, why is worship of the known God preferred?
A) Because the unknown effecter is doubtful.
B) Because the known effecter is more powerful.
C) Because the unknown effecter is impossible to exist.
D) Because the known effecter is the only necessary being.

Key Takeaway
In the scenario where multiple effects from one cause are not impossible, reason and revelation both direct us to worship only God, the known effecter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the known object of worship (God) versus any other thing you might rely on or seek help from, which is truly certain? Are there any 'unknown' objects of worship in your life—people, status, wealth—that you are giving obedience to? This lesson says reason demands you turn away from everything other than God. What effect would that have on your next decision?
?
The verse warns against invoking another god without proof. Is there any person or thing you 'invoke' in your heart—seeking security, approval, or identity—without clear proof from God? How can you confine yourself to the known God alone starting today?
?
This proof concludes that reason necessitates worship of the known, certain God. If you truly internalized that, what habit, relationship, or priority would change in your life this week? Be specific about what you will do.

The Second Proof for Tawheed: Second Division (Impossible Multiple Effects)
Razi presents the second division of the second proof for tawheed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second division of the second proof for tawheed: how the impossibility of multiple effects from one cause also leads to the conclusion that only one effecter exists.

Core Idea
If multiple effects from one cause are impossible, then no contingent can produce any effect.

Razi's second proof for tawheed continues with the alternative scenario: what if it is impossible for one cause to produce multiple effects? This lesson examines this branch of the argument. Razi shows that under this assumption, no contingent being can be an effecter, because that would require the impossible. Thus, only the Necessary Existent remains as the sole effecter.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Understand the assumption of the second division.
2
Follow the reductio argument
Trace why a contingent cannot be a source of an effect: its essence necessitates possibility, and if it necessitated another effect, that would be multiple effects from one cause.
This leads to a contradiction under the assumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إن عندهم البسيط لا يكون قابلاً وفاعلاً معاً . الحجة الثانية : أن نقول : إن الشيء الواحد . إما أن لا يمتنع كونه مصدراً للأثرين أو يمتنع . فإن لم يمتنع ذلك ، فنقول : لا شك أن واجب الوجود لذاته : موجود . ولا شك أنه مؤثر في وجود غيره . والتقدير في هذا القسم : أنه لا يمتنع صدور الآثار الكثيرة عن المؤثر الواحد . وإذا كان لم يمتنع إسناد جميع موجودات العالم إليه . وعلى هذا التقدير ، فإثبات المؤثر الواحد : معلوم ، وإما إثبات ما عداه : فمشكوك فيه . والتمسك بطاعة المعبود المعلوم، أولى من التمسك بطاعة المعبود المجهول . فثبت : أن العقل يقتضى التوجه إلى عبادة الله تعالى ، والإعراض عن كل ما سواه وهذا الدليل هو المذكور في الكتاب الإلهي ، حيث قال تعالى : ( ومن الله إلهاً آخر ، لا برهان له به. فإنما حسابه عند ربه ) والمعنى : أن يدع مع المعبود الأول معلوم الثبوت ، وما سواه غير معلوم. والاقتصار على المعلوم أولى من الذهاب إلى غير المعلوم وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يكون التقدير ، هو أنه يمتنع صدور الآثار الكثيرة عن المؤثر الواحد ، فنقول : فعلى هذا التقدير ، يمتنع كون الممكن لذاته ، مصدراً للأثر ، لأن للممكن لذاته ماهية ، تقتضي الإمكان فلو اقتضت تلك الماهية أثراً آخر ، لزم صدور الآثار الكثيرة عن المؤثر الواحد ، وهو محال .
Second: According to them, the simple is not receptive and active together. The second proof: We say: The single thing either is not impossible for it to be a source of two effects, or it is impossible. If that is not impossible, we say: There is no doubt that the Necessary Existent in itself exists. And there is no doubt that it effects the existence of other than itself. And the assumption in this division is that it is not impossible for many effects to issue from a single effecter. And if it is not impossible to attribute all existing things of the world to it. And on this assumption, the affirmation of a single effecter is known, but the affirmation of other than it is doubtful. And adherence to obedience of the known object of worship is more appropriate than adherence to obedience of the unknown object of worship. So it is established that reason necessitates directing oneself to worship of God Almighty and turning away from everything other than Him. And this proof is mentioned in the divine book, where He said: (And whoever invokes besides God another god for which he has no proof, then his reckoning is with his Lord). And the meaning is that one should leave the first object of worship whose existence is known, and other than it is unknown. And confining oneself to the known is more appropriate than going to the unknown. As for the second division: It is that the assumption is that it is impossible for many effects to issue from a single effecter. We say: On this assumption, it is impossible for that which is possible in itself to be a source of an effect, because that which is possible in itself has an essence that necessitates possibility. So if that essence necessitated another effect, the issuance of many effects from a single effecter would follow, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is a proof (the second proof) for tawheed (the oneness of God). It begins with a preliminary point stating that, according to the opponents, a simple entity cannot be both receptive and active simultaneously. Then the proof itself proceeds by dividing the issue of a single cause producing multiple effects into two possibilities: either it is not impossible or it is impossible. In the first case, the necessary existent (wajib al-wujud) is known to exist and to be an effecter of others. Since there is no impossibility in attributing all contingent things to it, affirming this single effecter is certain, while others are doubtful. Therefore, reason dictates worship of the known God alone. This is supported by the Quranic verse (23:117) which criticizes invoking another god without proof. In the second case, if it is impossible for one cause to produce multiple effects, then even a contingent thing (mumkin) cannot produce an effect, because its essence necessitates possibility, so any effect from it would require multiple effects from one cause, which is absurd. Thus, in both divisions, only one ultimate effecter remains.

Key Terms
مؤثر (effecter)
أثر (effect)
ممكن (contingent)
إمكان (possibility/contingency)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the impossibility of multiple effects would also apply to God, but the proof shows it eliminates contingent causes, leaving only God.
Correction: The assumption is about a single cause producing multiple effects; it does not apply to the Necessary Existent directly, but it shows contingent beings cannot be causes at all.

Checkpoint
Under the second assumption of the proof, why can't a contingent being be a source of an effect?
A) Because it would require multiple effects from one cause, which is impossible.
B) Because contingent beings are non-existent.
C) Because the necessary existent is the only cause.
D) Because the contingent's essence does not exist.

Key Takeaway
When multiple effects from one cause are impossible, no contingent can produce an effect, leaving only the Necessary Existent as the sole effecter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If only the Necessary Existent can be the true effecter, then what does that mean for your sense of personal agency? Are you willing to attribute every effect in your life—including your own actions—ultimately to Allah? How would that change your humility and reliance on Him starting today?
?
Consider something you believe you have achieved through your own effort. According to this proof, your essence cannot produce that effect. How does this reframe your gratitude? Will you consciously thank Allah not just for the outcome but for every step of causation you thought was yours?
?
This proof strips away any claim of independent causal power from you. Does that feel liberating or unsettling? Examine your heart: is there any part of you that resists surrendering the illusion of being a 'source' of effects? What would it cost you to truly believe that only Allah is the effecter?

The Third Proof: Contingency Necessitates a Specific Cause
Razi presents the third proof that contingency is the sole cause of need for an effecter, leading to a single specific cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why contingency must necessitate a single specific effecter, leading to the conclusion of oneness.

Core Idea
Contingency alone causes need and demands a specific effecter.

This passage presents the third proof for the oneness of the effecter. Razi argues that contingency is the sole cause of need for an effecter, and because contingency is one thing, it necessitates a specific effecter—not an unspecified one. This establishes that every contingent being depends on one unique cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the complete argument
Read the Arabic passage and the full translation. Notice the structure: claim, evidence, conclusion.
The proof is stated concisely.
2
Identify the claim about contingency
The proof begins by stating that contingency is the cause of need. Follow the reasoning: if we remove contingency, only necessity or impossibility remain, both of which eliminate need.
This shows contingency is the sole cause.
3
Understand the move to specificity
Since contingency is one concept, the need it causes must be for something specific. An unspecified effecter cannot exist in itself, so it cannot be the cause.
4
Grasp the final conclusion
Therefore, every contingent thing is attributed to that one specific effecter, establishing that there is no effecter but the One.
This is the conclusion of the third proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إن علة الحاجة إلى المؤثر، هي الإمكان . والدليل عليه : إنا إذا رفعنا الإمكان عن الوهم ، بقي الوجوب بالذات ، أو الامتناع بالذات ، وكل واحد منهما ، يحيل الحاجة إلى المؤثر. فثبت : أن علة الحاجة ليست إلا الإمكان . والمفهوم من الإمكان أمر واحد ، فعلة الحاجة إلى المؤثر أمر واحد . وذلك الأمر الواحد ، إما أن يكون علة للحاجة إلى مؤثر معين ، أو إلى مؤثر غير معين . والثاني باطل ، لأن المؤشر الذي لا يكون معيناً في ذاته امتنع وجوده في نفسه [ لأن كل ما كان موجوداً في نفسه ] فهو معين في ذاته ، وما لا يكون معيناً في ذاته ، امتنع كونه موجوداً في ذاته ، وما لا وجود له في ذاته ، امتنع احتياج غيره في الوجود إليه . فثبت : أن الإمكان لا يحوج إلا إلى شيء معين . فوجب إسناد كل ممكن إليه . فثبت : أنه لا مؤثر إلا الواحد . فهذا تقرير هذا القول
The third proof: The cause of need for an effecter is contingency. The evidence for it: If we remove contingency from the mind, necessity in itself or impossibility in itself remains, and each of them precludes the need for an effecter. So it is established that the cause of need is nothing but contingency. And the concept of contingency is one thing, so the cause of need for an effecter is one thing. That one thing is either a cause of need for a specific effecter or for an unspecified effecter. The second is false, because an effecter that is not specific in its essence is impossible in its existence [because everything that exists in itself is specific in its essence], and what is not specific in its essence is impossible for it to exist in itself, and what has no existence in itself is impossible for other than it to need it for existence. So it is established that contingency does not necessitate except something specific. Therefore, it is necessary to attribute every contingent thing to it. So it is established that there is no effecter except the One. This is the exposition of this statement.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage contains the third proof (al-hujja al-thalitha) for the oneness of the necessary effecter. It begins by stating that the cause of the need for an effecter is contingency (imkan). The proof is: if we remove contingency from consideration, only necessity (wujub) or impossibility (imtina') remain, both of which preclude the need for an effecter. Therefore, contingency alone causes the need. Since contingency is a single concept, the cause of need is one thing. This one thing (contingency) must necessitate a specific (mu'ayyan) effecter, not an unspecified one. The argument then shows that an unspecified effecter cannot exist in itself, because any existing thing must be specific. Thus, contingency necessitates a specific effecter. Consequently, every contingent thing must be attributed to that specific effecter, leading to the conclusion that there is no effecter but the One. This concludes the exposition of this position.

Key Terms
علة (cause)
حاجة (need)
مؤثر (effecter)
إمكان (contingency)
وجوب (necessity)
امتناع (impossibility)
معين (specific)
موجود (existent)
ذات (essence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Contingency could necessitate multiple possible effecters or an unspecified one.
Correction: The proof shows that contingency, being one concept, necessitates a specific effecter; an unspecified effecter cannot exist in itself, so it cannot be the cause.

Checkpoint
According to the third proof, what is the sole cause of the need for an effecter?
A) Necessity in itself.
B) Contingency.
C) Impossibility in itself.
D) Existence in itself.

Key Takeaway
Contingency alone necessitates a single specific effecter, proving the oneness of the cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your very existence is contingent and demands a single specific Cause, how often do you live as if you are self-sufficient? Identify one moment today where you acted as if you didn't need that Cause—and commit to replacing that feeling with conscious dependence on Him.
?
The proof declares that 'there is no effecter except the One.' Yet you often attribute outcomes to your own effort, luck, or other people. Right now, recall a recent success or failure. Can you honestly say you saw the exclusive causality of the One in it? What would it cost you to consistently see Him as the only true effecter?
?
An unspecified effecter is impossible—meaning your trust cannot be placed in vague forces or multiple powers. What 'unspecified effecters' do you still rely on (e.g., chance, time, people's goodwill)? How will you train your heart to direct all reliance to that One specific Cause?

Why Every Existent Must Either Affect or Be Affected
The author proves that a being which neither affects nor is affected cannot exist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why reason proves that no existent can be completely inert, neither causing nor receiving effects.

Core Idea
Every existent is either a cause or an effect — there is no third option.

This lesson presents a concise logical argument from the author. Building on previously established truths — that every existent is either necessary or possible, that the Necessary Being is one, and that every possible is caused — the author demonstrates that the category of a 'completely passive' being is rationally impossible. This passage is a model of deductive reasoning in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premises
Review the three key premises: every existent is either necessary or possible; the necessary is one; every possible is caused. These are established earlier in the text.
These premises are taken as given in this argument.
2
Apply the premises to the fourth division
Consider the claim of an existent that neither affects nor is affected. Test it against the premises: if it is necessary, it must affect (since the Necessary is the cause); if it is possible, it must be affected (since every possible is caused).
3
Draw the conclusion
Since the fourth division fails both tests, it is impossible. There is no existent that is neither effecter nor affected.
The argument is a proof by division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسم الرابع من أقسام الموجودات الموجود الذي لا يؤثر ولا يتأثر البتة : وهذا القسم ممتنع الوجود في العقول . فإنا لما دللنا على أن الموجود ، إما واجب ، وإما ممكن . ودللنا على أن الواجب : واحد . ودللنا على أن كل ممكن : فهو معلول . فحينئذ يكون ذلك الواجب الواحد مؤثراً فيه . وإذا ثبت هذا ، ظهر أن الموجود ، إن كان واجباً لذاته، فهو مؤثر . وإن كان ممكناً لذاته ، فهو متأثر . فالقول بإثبات موجود لا يكون مؤثراً ولا متأثراً : محال .
And the fourth division of the divisions of existents: the existent that neither affects nor is affected at all. And this division is impossible in intellects. For when we have proved that the existent is either necessary or possible, and we have proved that the necessary is one, and we have proved that every possible is caused, then that one necessary being is an effecter in it. And when this is established, it becomes clear that the existent, if it is necessary by itself, then it is an effecter; and if it is possible by itself, then it is affected. So the statement asserting an existent that is neither effecter nor affected is impossible.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a proof by division. The fourth division of existents—a being that neither causes effects nor receives effects—is declared impossible by reason. The author reviews previously established premises: every existent is either necessary or possible. The necessary is one (God). Every possible is caused. Therefore, the necessary being (God) is an effecter in relation to the possible. Hence, if something is necessary, it is an effecter; if it is possible, it is affected. There is no room for a being that is neither. Therefore, the claim of such a being is impossible.

Key Terms
القسم الرابع
مؤثر
متأثر
واجب
ممكن
معلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God, being unaffected, is also not an effecter, that is, completely passive.
Correction: The passage clarifies that being necessary (as God is) entails being the effecter of all possible beings. Necessity implies active causation, not passivity.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what is the status of a possible being?
A) It is an effecter
B) It is affected
C) It is both effecter and affected
D) It is neither

Key Takeaway
The fourth division of existents — a being that neither affects nor is affected — is rationally impossible because every existent is either necessary (and thus an effecter) or possible (and thus affected).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that only Allah is the true effecter, why do you still fear people or circumstances as if they have independent power to affect you? What would change if you lived this truth daily?
?
You are a possible being, constantly affected. Does your heart accept this dependence, or do you resent it? Will you embrace being 'affected' by Allah’s commands and seek His effecting, or do you try to be independent?
?
The proof shows that any existent outside of Allah is affected. Have you ever acted as if you could affect your own destiny without needing Allah? How can you realign your actions with the reality that you are always the one affected, not the effecter?

First Proof: Impossibility of Non-Bodily Possible Existents
Theologians' first proof against non-bodily possible existents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theologians' first proof that it is impossible to prove the existence of any possible being that is neither a body nor indwelling in a body, and why this argument guards the uniqueness of God.

Core Idea
Sharing God's unique negative attributes would make another being equal to God in essence.

Theologians faced a challenge: if God is non-corporeal and not in a body, could there be other spiritual beings? This lesson unpacks their first proof, a reductio argument that shows why such beings cannot be possible existents without collapsing into polytheism or making God a mere possible being.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument unfold naturally.
Notice the technical terms: متحيز (body), حال في المتحيز (indwelling in a body).
2
Identify the reductio structure
The argument assumes a scenario (a non-bodily possible existent) and shows it leads to two impossible conclusions. Identify the premise, the supposition, and the two consequences.
The two consequences are: either all are necessary existents or all are possible existents.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Why does the theologians' proof conclude impossibility? Connect the logical steps back to the core idea: sharing God's distinguishing attributes leads to equality in quiddity.
This proof is specifically about possible existents, not necessary ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زعم أكثر المتكلمين : أن إثبات موجود ممكن الوجود ، لا يكون متحيزاً ، ولا حالا في المتحيز : محال . واحتجوا عليه بوجوه :
الحجة الأولى : قالوا : ثبت بالدليل : أن إله العالم [ يجب أن ] لا يكون متحيزاً ، ولا حالاً في المتحيز . فلو فرضنا موجوداً آخر بهذه الصفة ، لكان الموجود : مساوياً لذات الله تعالى في أنه غير متحيز ، ولا حال في المتحيز . والإستواء في هذا الحكم ، يوجب الإستواء في الماهية . بدليل أنا إذا أردنا أن نذكر في ذات الله تعالى : صفة ، بإعتبارها تمتاز ذاته عن سائر الذوات ، لم نقدر إلا على ذكر هذه الصفة. وهي : أنه ذات ليست بمتحيزة ، ولا حالة في شيء من المتحيزات . والصفة إذا كانت كاشفة عن الحقيقة ، كان الإشتراك فيها ، يوجب الإشتراك في الحقيقة . فثبت : أنه لو حصل موجود بهذه الصفة ، لكان ذلك الموجود مثيلا لذات الله تعالى . والمثلان يجب استواؤ هما في جميع اللوازم . فيلزم : إما القول يكون الكل : آلهة واجبة الوجود ، أو بكون الكل عبيداً ممكنة الوجود . ولما كان الكل محالاً . ثبت : أن إثبات موجود بهذه الصفة . محال .
Most of the theologians claimed: that proving an existent which is possible of existence, which is not a body (mutahayyiz), nor indwelling in a body (hallun fi l-mutahayyiz), is impossible. And they argued for it with proofs. The first proof: They said: It is established by proof that the God of the world must not be a body, nor indwelling in a body. So if we suppose another existent with this attribute, then the existent would be equal to the essence of God Almighty in that it is neither a body nor indwelling in a body. Equality in this ruling necessitates equality in quiddity (mahiyyah). The evidence is that if we wish to mention an attribute of the essence of God Almighty by virtue of which His essence is distinguished from other essences, we are not able except to mention this attribute, namely: that He is an essence which is not a body and not indwelling in any of the bodies. And if the attribute is disclosive of the reality, then sharing in it necessitates sharing in the reality. So it is established that if there were an existent with this attribute, that existent would be a similitude (mithl) of the essence of God Almighty. And two similars must be equal in all concomitants. So it follows either that all are gods necessary of existence (wajibat al-wujud), or that all are servants possible of existence (mumkinat al-wujud). And since all of that is impossible, it is established that proving an existent with this attribute is impossible.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof used by most theologians to argue that it is impossible to prove the existence of a possible being that is neither a body (mutahayyiz) nor indwelling in a body (hāllun fī l-mutahayyiz) – i.e., a spiritual being distinct from God. The argument proceeds as follows: First, it is established by proof that God is not a body nor indwelling in a body. If we suppose another existent with the same two negative attributes (non-corporeal and not indwelling), then that existent would be equal to God in these attributes. Equality in a ruling that distinguishes God from all other things (since only God has these attributes) would necessitate equality in quiddity (mahiyya). The authors argue that the only attribute that distinguishes God from other essences is precisely these two negative attributes: not being a body and not indwelling in a body. If another being shares this distinguishing attribute, then it shares in the reality (haqīqa) of God, meaning it would be a similitude (mithl) of God. But two similars must be equal in all concomitants (lawāzim). This leads to two impossible consequences: either both are necessary existents (wājib al-wujūd) – resulting in multiple gods – or both are possible existents (mumkin al-wujūd) – making God a mere possible being. Both conclusions are impossible, therefore the original supposition of a non-corporeal possible existent is impossible. The argument is a reductio ad absurdum, showing the theological difficulty of accepting any spiritual being that shares God's unique negative attributes.

Key Terms
ممكن الوجود
متحيز
حال في المتحيز
ماهية
مثلان
واجب الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument denies the existence of any spiritual being (angels, jinn) altogether.
Correction: The argument only targets possible existents and does not deny beings that are bodies (e.g., angels with subtle bodies) or those that are necessary (God). It specifically shows that a possible being sharing God's unique negative attributes leads to absurdity.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the theologians' first proof?
A) Spiritual beings are impossible because they would be equal to God.
B) Proving a possible existent that is neither a body nor in a body is impossible.
C) God cannot be a body, so spiritual beings are possible.
D) Two non-corporeal beings must be equal in all respects.

Key Takeaway
The theologians' first proof establishes that no possible being can share God's unique negative attributes, thus preserving divine uniqueness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If no other being can share God's unique attributes, examine your attachments. Is there anything—wealth, status, a person—that you implicitly treat as having God's exclusive power or control? What would it take to uproot that from your heart?
?
The theologians used this argument to protect tawhid. Consider a moment when you attributed to a created being a quality that belongs only to God (e.g., ultimate security, knowledge of the future). How did that affect your relationship with Him? What practical step can you take today to redirect that trust back to Allah alone?
?
The proof shows that sharing God's distinguishing attributes leads to absurdity. Reflect on your worship: does any part of your prayer or devotion inadvertently associate God's unique attributes with something else? Ask yourself: Is my worship purely for Him, or have I allowed something to share that exclusivity?

The First Argument and Its Refutation
First argument and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theologians' first argument against non-bodily contingent existents and the key refutation that equality in negative attributes does not imply equality in quiddity.

Core Idea
Equality in negative attributes does not prove equality in essence.

The first argument attempts to show that any non-bodily contingent being would be a likeness of God. The refutation exposes a crucial fallacy: shared negations do not determine the full reality. This lesson presents the argument and its rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the first argument carefully
Read the argument from the beginning of 'al-hujja al-ula' to the conclusion that such an existent is impossible. Note each logical step.
The argument proceeds from shared negative attribute to shared essence to likeness to impossible consequences.
2
Understand the refutation
Read the refutation which argues that equality in negative attributes (sifa salbiyya) does not necessitate equality in the full quiddity. Two proofs are given: every two realities share in the negation of everything else, and two species under one genus share the genus but are not absolutely alike.
This refutation undermines the core inference of the argument.
3
Evaluate the strength of the argument
Reflect on whether the refutation successfully shows that the first argument is weak. Consider if the theologians' claim that the negative attribute is the distinguishing characteristic is refuted by the fact that many things share the same negative attributes.
