The Three Possibilities for Human Souls
Al-Razi enumerates three possibilities for human souls and dismisses the first two.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three possible positions regarding the nature of human rational souls and why the first two are rejected.

Core Idea
Human souls are neither necessary nor eternal but contingent and originated.

Al-Razi begins by laying out the logical possibilities for human souls: they could be necessary, eternal but not necessary, or contingent and originated. He rapidly dismisses the first two, clearing the way for the third position which he will defend.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of views
Read the Arabic passage where Al-Razi lists three possibilities: necessary, eternal, contingent. Understand the phrasing of each.
Pay attention to the wording 'واجبة الوجود لذواتها' vs 'قديمة أزلية'.
2
Examine the refutation of the first view
Notice that Al-Razi dismisses the first view by citing proofs that only the One is necessary. This is a brief reference to earlier arguments.
3
Examine the refutation of the second view
He also dismisses the second view as already discussed. This indicates a prior argument against the eternity of souls.
This sets up the third view as the viable option.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم : أن هذه النفوس البشرية . فيها ثلاث مراتب في الاحتمالات : أحدها : أن نقول إنها ليست محدثة . وليست أيضاً ممكنة . بل هي أشياء واجبة الوجود لذواتها . وثانيها : أن يقال إنها ليست واجبة الوجود لذواتها ، إلا أنها قديمة أزلية . كما يقول الفلاسفة في العقول العقلية والنفوس الفلكية . وثالثها: أن يقال : إنها لا واجبة ولا أزلية ، بل هي ممكنة لذواتها ، محدثة حدوثاً زمانياً . أما القول الأول : فالدليل على بطلانه : الدلائل المذكورة في أن واجب الوجود لذاته ، ليس إلا الواحد . وأما القول الثاني : وهي أنها قديمة . فالقول فيه قد سبق . وأما القول الثالث : وهو أنها ممكنة لذواتها ، محدثة زمانيا فنقول : لما ثبت أنها ممكنة لذواتها . فسواء قلنا : إنها قديمة أو محدثة . فإنه لا بد لها من مؤثر وموجد ، وذلك الموجد إما أن يكون متحيزاً ، أو حالا في المتحيز أو لا متحيزاً ولا حالا في المتحيز . لا جائز أن يكون متحيزاً لوجوه : الأول : إنا بينا : أن المتحيزات متماثلة في تمام الماهية. فلو كان واحد منها علة لشيء ، لكان كل واحد منها علة لمثل ذلك الشيء . وذلك باطل . والثاني : إن الفلاسفة يقولون : إن الشيء الواحد ، لا يكون قابلاً وفاعلاً معاً ، والأجسام قابلة ، فوجب أن لا تكون فاعلة . والثالث : إن المتحيز أضعف وجوداً من الجوهر المجرد لأن المتحيز محتاج إلى المكان والجهة ، والمجرد غني عنهما . والأضعف لا يكون علة للأقوى . والرابع : إن النفوس البشرية عالمة بالحقائق ، قادرة على الأفعال . والجسم من حيث إنه جسم ، ليس كذلك. فالنفوس أشرف من الأجسام ، والأشرف لا يكون معلولاً للأخس . والخامس : إن الأجسام إنما تؤثر بمشاركة الوضع . والمراد من هذا الوضع : أن المؤثر الجسماني يؤثر في القريب منه أولا . ثم يؤثر ثانياً فيها اتصل بذلك القريب . ثم يؤثر ثالثا فيها اتصل بذلك الثاني . وهذا هو المراد من قولنا : إن المؤثر الجسماني إنما يؤثر بواسطة الوضع . والدليل على أن الأمر كذلك : هو أنه لو لم يكن الأمر كذلك لكان تأثير هذا المؤثر الجسماني في القريب والبعيد سواء . ولما لم يكن الأمر كذلك علمنا : أنه إنما يؤثر بمشاركة الوضع. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : الذي يمكن وصفه بالبعد والقرب من الجسم
Know that these human souls have three ranks of possibilities: One of them: that we say they are not originated, nor are they possible, but they are things necessary of existence in themselves. The second: that it is said they are not necessary of existence in themselves, but they are eternal, pre-eternal, as the philosophers say about the intellects and the celestial souls. The third: that it is said they are neither necessary nor eternal, but they are possible in themselves, originated temporally. As for the first statement: the proof of its falsehood is the proofs mentioned that the necessary of existence in Itself is only the One. As for the second statement, which is that they are eternal: the discussion about it has preceded. As for the third statement, which is that they are possible in themselves, temporally originated: we say: since it is established that they are possible in themselves, then whether we say they are eternal or originated, they inevitably have an influencer and a bringer into existence. That bringer into existence is either a body (mutaḥayyiz), or a state in a body, or neither a body nor a state in a body. It is not permissible that it be a body, for reasons: First: we have shown that bodies are similar in entirety of quiddity. If one of them were a cause of something, then each one of them would be a cause of the like of that thing, and that is false. Second: the philosophers say that one thing cannot be both receptive and agent simultaneously, and bodies are receptive, so they must not be agent. Third: a body is weaker in existence than an immaterial substance (jawhar mujarrad), because a body needs place and direction, while the immaterial is free from both. The weaker cannot be a cause of the stronger. Fourth: human souls are knowledgeable of realities, capable of actions. A body, insofar as it is a body, is not like that. Souls are nobler than bodies, and the nobler cannot be an effect of the baser. Fifth: bodies only have effect by association of position. The meaning of this position is that a corporeal influencer influences first what is near it, then secondarily influences what is connected to that near thing, then thirdly influences what is connected to that second. That is the meaning of our saying: the corporeal influencer only influences by means of position. The proof that the matter is so is that if the matter were not so, the influence of this corporeal influencer on the near and the far would be equal. Since the matter is not so, we know that it only influences by association of position. And when this is established, we say: that which can be described by distance and proximity to the body...
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation. The author, likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, first enumerates three possible positions regarding human rational souls (al-nufus al-natiqah): (1) they are necessary of existence in themselves (i.e., part of the Necessary Existent), (2) they are not necessary but are eternal (as the philosophers claim for celestial intellects and souls), or (3) they are contingent (mumkin) and temporally originated (muhdath zamanan). He then dismisses the first position by citing proofs that only the One is necessary of existence. The second position he says has already been discussed. He then takes up the third position: since the souls are contingent, they require an agent (mu'aththir) and originator (mujid). That agent must either be a body (mutaḥayyiz), an accident in a body, or neither a body nor an accident. He argues that it cannot be a body, providing five reasons: (1) Bodies are similar in quiddity; if one were a cause, all would be, which is false. (2) A single thing cannot be both receptive and agent; bodies are receptive, so they cannot be agents. (3) Bodies are weaker than immaterial substances; the weaker cannot cause the stronger. (4) Souls are nobler (knowing, powerful) than bodies; the nobler cannot be an effect of the baser. (5) Bodies only act via spatial position (wad'), influencing near things first; this requires position, but the agent of souls is not spatial. The fifth proof includes an argument that if bodies acted without position, they would affect near and far equally, which is not observed. The text cuts off mid-sentence, so the conclusion is incomplete, but the argument clearly denies that the agent is a body.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود (necessary existent)
ممكن (contingent)
قديم (eternal)
محدث (originated)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi, what is the only possible view about human souls that remains after dismissing the first two?
A) They are necessary of existence.
B) They are eternal but not necessary.
C) They are contingent and originated.
D) They are part of the celestial intellects.

Key Takeaway
Human souls are contingent and temporally originated, not necessary or eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that your soul is not necessary or eternal, but contingent and created by God. In what specific areas of your life have you been living as if you are self-sufficient (necessary) or as if your soul is eternal and independent? What would change if you truly internalized that you exist only by God's will and could cease to exist at any moment?
?
Al-Razi dismisses the view that souls are eternal. Yet we often act as if our existence is permanent—delaying repentance, putting off good deeds, or ignoring our mortality. How would your daily choices—your sleep, your speech, your time—shift if you deeply knew that your soul had a definite beginning and will have a definite end?
?
The philosophers claimed souls are eternal, but this lesson teaches they are originated. Are there beliefs or habits you hold that treat your soul as though it is self-originating or independent of God? What is one concrete step you can take today to 'originate' a new practice that acknowledges your utter dependence on Allah?
